 3046 or 3047

 English/Maths GCSE highest prior attainment grade for the previous year is missing or invalid.

 These errors appear when the grade at last census is blank. Ensure that the grade at last census for both GCSE English and GCSE Maths contains a mark.

 If their grade has not changed, you will still need to input their grade at last census as the same.

 Please note that this will not automatically carry over from previous years. You will need to add in this information for each year - use the academic year drop-down menu to change between years.

 ‚Ä¢ Pupils with SEND (both those receiving support and those with Education, Health and Care (EHC) plans)

 ‚Ä¢ Pupils known or previously known to children‚Äôs social care

 ‚Ä¢ Pupils who face other barriers to learning or wellbeing (which may include protected characteristics, adverse circumstances, or contextual vulnerabilities)

 Inspectors will expect schools to show how they adapt practice to meet these pupils‚Äô needs, how they monitor outcomes, and how they evidence impact - not merely intent.

 Currently, Arbor classifies a student as ‚Äúdisadvantaged‚Äù if they have ever been eligible for Free School Meals (FSM) in the past six years or are/looked-after by the local authority.

 To better support schools under the new Ofsted regime, Arbor could evolve this functionality to reflect the broader and more nuanced definition of disadvantage.

 ## Arbor Education Partners ##

 Hi Nadia,

 Thanks for getting in touch!

 If staff members overwrite a planned absence with a present mark, the note that was attached will no longer be visible. This is expected behaviour because when you overwrite the absence, the system takes the most recently added mark, which can remove any previously added notes.

 It may be worth looking at alternative options for notes to staff for these kinds of notifications.

 I would also recommend leaving feedback to our Product Team via the below process around this.

 Our team at Arbor is unable to submit suggestions on behalf of schools, as we want to ensure the full impact and needs of your school have been reflected in the suggestion. We appreciate this can be more time-consuming than you would hope, but it will help us to improve our product for all schools.

 How do I submit feedback?

 You can submit your feedback to our Roadmap directly in Arbor.

 Head to Help & Learn with Arbor in the left-hand menu > Share product idea to tell us how an existing feature could be improved, or share an idea for a new way that Arbor could save you time.

 Please make sure to include as much detail as possible, as it helps our Product Team to prioritise and understand your idea. You can submit your product ideas from the School and/or MAT MIS.

 What next?

 ‚Ä¢ Our Product Team runs a termly roadmap planning process.

 ‚Ä¢ Once a term, we analyse the ideas our customers have submitted and look for patterns and themes to give us an understanding of the features that would have the most impact for our customers.

 ‚Ä¢ You won‚Äôt hear from our Product Team unless they need more information. They will be working behind the scenes to consider if your suggestion is possible with current plans

 You can see all the work our Product Team has released recently in our Change Log.

 Let me know if you need anything else and I‚Äôll be happy to help.

 All the best,

 Jade Taylor

 Advanced Support Customer Success Analyst

Ticket: PFT-5656
Issue id: 193352
Module: Behaviour
Summary: Colours in Behaviour charts are fixed and therefore unhelpful - Negative points are showing as green, positive as red.
Role: MIS Assistant
Source: Sheet1 - Row 239
Comment: Despite directionality being set up correctly within Point Awards, the colours that each point appears in on behaviour graphs is fixed. This is causing a lot of confusion within our staff body as, visually, it looks like students in this school have more negative than positive as the natural association with these colours are green=good, red/orange=bad.

 PLEASE allow users to choose the colour for the 5 categories that are shown in each Reg Form's behaviour graph: Positive Incidents, Negative Incidents, Negative Points, Positive Points, Detentions.

 Even if you have to keep the default Arbor colour scheme, please can we choose which of these colours we assign to which category. Both shades of green work for positive points and incidents, and I could cope with yellow and orange for negative points and incidents. Red for detentions is fine.

 But at the moment, our 'negative points' is currently green. I spoke to Arbor support about this and they said it will likely be related to the order the points were set up. In one of our other schools (I work for the MAT), Positive points is green so this makes for a graph that makes more visual sense. There is no indicator when setting up point awards that creating one before the other would impact these colours; I thought this would be tied to 'directionality' which makes a bit more sense, but it isn't! It's related to a fixed order which is quite arbitrary as it's likely a 50/50 split between people who put create negative first and people who create positive first - this is random and should not have an impact on anything fixed that they can't change, especially when choosing a 'directionality' is an option. I'd even accept directionality choice dictating the colours.

 This difference in colours across our schools also makes comparison virtually impossible as the graph colours look different across each school. Some have lots of green, some have no green whatsoever, some have mostly orange - no consistent key can be applied across schools and visually it cannot be interpreted for multiple schools at the same time when they appear so differently. And we don't just want to delete the existing point awards to create them in a different order as this will remove historic points, and we have reports etc tied to these points so this isn't an option for us.

 Thank you for reading my concerns; I really hope this is actioned as it's causing a lot of confusion amongst staff and stifling our behaviour comparison between our schools.

Ticket: PFT-5520

Module: Behaviour
Summary: Detention system
Role: Assistant Head of Behaviour
Source: Sheet1 - Row 375
Comment: *+Current problem+*

 I am trying to set up a detention system and I have run into a problem with the way that Arbor handles detention double booking to next available session. The detention system works like a calendar where you cannot double book students. Anyone who gets multiple detentions for the same time will automatically be sent to the next available session of that type.

 E.g. Student X gets a 30 minute detention in one lesson, an hour in another and misses their homework earning them another 30 minutes. Because they are all for the same time, they sit the 30 minute behaviour one day, the hour the next day and the homework detention after that.

 Idea:

 Allowing an option when selecting 'Next available session' in the work flow set up that allows multiple sessions to be run at the same time and defaults to the longest detention set that day for register purposes.

Ticket: PFT-5512
Issue id: 192882
Module: Payments
Summary: Ability to pay for school Shop Items by Cash
Role: Support Partner
Source: Sheet1 - Row 383
Comment: I raised call asking why schools cannot make payments for School Shop items by cash.

 Some items on school shop are of low monetary value, particularly in Primary Schools and therefore to pay by card is not cost effective to schools. Also some parents do not have cards and can only pay by cash.

 Schools are asking how they can record the sales of these items therefore in Arbor to ensure that their payments are all accounted for.

 The response I received from 2nd line was :

 " that the School Shop was built for payments to be taken via the Parent Portal, which only allows card payments, so parents can only pay by card for the Products"

 And a workaround as follows was offered:

 There is a way around this, though, albeit a little long-winded:

 If the parents are only able to pay by cash, the school can deposit the money for each item in their school bank account, and then essentially purchase the Product for the parents. When they enter the card details for paying for the item, they can then add the school card details.

 For recording the sale of the items to ensure the payments are accounted for, when a parent purchases a School Shop item, they can mark the item as issued. This allows them to keep track of how many of the items they have sold.

 Any payments for School Shop items will show in their Settlement Statement, and they can reconcile their School Shop orders via School > Payments > School Shop > School Shop Orders.

 However, to feed back up the line, in a lot of schools this workaround is not an option because if a school wants to use a a school card, particularly if part of a trust, they have to submit a request and put in a purchase order, giving 3 days notice to the finance officer before they can even use the card to make the payment üòí

 If it is an option for Meals, Clubs & Trips, staff, parents and ourselves cannot understand why it is not an option for School Shop too.

 Many thanks in advance

 Kind regards,

 Deborah

Ticket: PFT-5496
Issue id: 192770
Module: Behaviour
Summary: Interventions - Not timetabled & Detentions Delay timings
Role: Deputy Head
Source: Sheet1 - Row 399
Comment: Good afternoon,

 I would appreciate it that serious consideration is given to these two ideas.

 1. Recording interventions which are not timetable based. I would like to see a set up similar that of behaviour incident recording which allows for adhoc addition of interventions and support strategies which are not timetabled activities. For example, I would like to be able to customise a series of interventions which are assigned a tiered level.

 Examples - Tutor behaviour report started, Tutor behaviour report ended, Tutor behaviour report escaleted to Year Leader Report etc, EHCP Review meeting, Behaviour Meeting parent, IBP Commenced, IBP Review. IBP closed. IBP Escalated to PSP.

 These would be inputted to a similar data entry system as the behaviour logging.

 Then a timeline could be created of support provided to each pupil which can be combined with the timetabled interventions in the current system.

 2. I have requested this previously but has not been actioned. The 24hour delay on detentions does not work adequately for schools that set lunchtime detentions which are set in the afternoon. For example. If I set a pupil a lunch detention at 9am in the morning with a 24hr delay that lunch detention will be set for 12.00pm the following day. If I set the child a detention at 1.00pm on a Monday, the 24 hour delay will mean that detention will not be sat until Wednesday.

 The simple solution is to set a 12hr delay or a next day delay. At the moment I have to fudge the timings to accommodate this issue by telling the system the lunch detention is at 5pm and the afterschool detention is at 6.00pm.

 Would really appreciate some consideration of these suggestions and happy to discuss and explain in further detail.

Source: Sheet1 - Row 525
Comment: Previously we had SIMS and we were able to take an emergency fire drill which was a register that could be taken in the event of a fire but had no impact on the actual registers.

 At the end of the drill you can just reset the register.

 It is hard to explain but I do have a process document I can share should you need the actual process that was involved.

 Currently with Arbor we are having to revert to a less efficient method which is not ideal.

Module: Parent Portal/App

Role: Family Engagement Worker
Source: Sheet1 - Row 554
Comment: Hello,

 Our school and college have recently started using the parent in-app messaging service and, while it has great potential, we have experienced several challenges. Moving forward, I would like to suggest improvements that would make this form of communication more accessible and effective for parents, carers, and school staff.

 In our SEN school and college, daily communication with families is essential, and it is important that staff can both send and view replies. To ensure this, we would like to recommend the following updates:

 Safeguarding: Only class teachers should be able to view the messages related to their class.

 Notifications: Class teachers should receive direct notifications for messages relevant to their class.

 Accessibility for Families: The app should support multiple languages so that all families can access and understand the communication.

 These improvements would make a significant difference in ensuring safe, accessible, and effective communication between school and families.

 Thank you for considering these updates, and we look forward to seeing how the service can be developed further.

 Georgina Williams

Role: Trust Data Manager
Source: Sheet1 - Row 574
Comment: Hi, these are 2 separate funds that we cannot use in the same way. It really complicates things when staff cannot rely on the PPG data for analysis or to know who is entitled to trip subsidies, etc. Please change this so Service Children are not automatically counted as PPG!! Here is the link to the guidance and here is the extract

 https://www.gov.uk/government/publications/the-service-pupil-premium/service-pupil-premium-what-you-need-to-know#:~:text=%C2%A9%20Crown%20copyright%202025,%C2%A3350%20per%20service%20child.

 **How SPP differs from the Pupil Premium (PP)**

 SPP helps schools provide mainly pastoral support for service children. The Pupil Premium (PP) was introduced to raise attainment and accelerate progress within disadvantaged groups.

 Schools should not combine SPP with PP funding: the spending of each premium should be accounted for separately, but schools can be allocated both SPP and PP for the same child if they are eligible for both.

 Thanks

 Natalie

 No, if your school is using a two-week timetable, it is not possible to assign staff members to detentions on alternating weeks, or have different detentions on alternating weeks.

Ticket: PFT-5058
Issue id: 191226
Module: Groups & Enrolments
Summary: Admin to take and process a Cash payment in the school shop
Role: Data Manager
Source: Sheet1 - Row 837
Comment: Hi, would it be possible to add a feature to the school shop payments? We have quite a few items in our school shop, we ask all parents to buy items from this area on their card. There are times where a parent can not purchase these items for various reasons vis the school shop. There are times where the office will sell an item and receive cash. At present we are not able to process a sale with cash a form of payment, it will only process a sale on a card.

 Reasons how this will help us:

 1) Some of the items in the shop for example our school sweatshirts, have a stock amount. We use the current stock to tell how many jumpers we have left in stock. If we sell a jumper using cash this then causes us problems with stock control.

 2) We have a voluntary contribution that we ask ALL parents to make towards Art supplies. This currently is an item in the school shop. We have had to take some cash payments for this item and now can not tell who still needs to pay when we download the list of purchases.

 FYI - The school is in a deprived area and for some of our parents, cash is the only viable option. We also have a lot of parents who are EAL and struggle to can not use the school app.

 Of course there are work arounds but this creates a lot of manual admin time and becomes a more manual process where a Cash payment would stop us having to create spreadsheets to track it.

 A suggestion on how this could be used, only admin staff in the school can process a shop item with a cash payment. We would still only want the parents to purchase these items on card.

 Please note - receiving cash is a last resort. We would prefer the parents to purchase all items using their card using the school shop.

 I really hope this feature request will go ahead as we have struggled with this issue for a few years now.

 Many thanks - Louise

Ticket: PFT-5057
Issue id: 191225
Module: Payments
Summary: Planned absence notes automatically moved to register
Role: School Business and Finance Manager
Source: Sheet1 - Row 838
Comment: After a live chat with your team:

 "Whilst that data has pulled through, I can confirm that the reason that the Planned Absence doesn't show up in the register is because of how it was created (for both students)

 This planned absence is classed as a narrative (note) associated with a planned absence and these two form of notes don't appear the same on registers.

 This means that planned absence notes won't show the same as lesson attendance notes but the best way to see how both of these display (and which is which) is on the Bulk Edit Marks Advanced page.

 You can also add notes from this page so the note will appear in Students > Attendance > Registers > Daily Attendance as you expected. "

 **However, I can see how this would be useful for your school to have both notes display in the same way on the register so this would be a great idea for our Product team to look into further.**
